SECOND FAMILY HEALTH PROJECT
Draft Terms of Reference for Consultant/Trainer
to Work with Nutrition Unit for KOH
Introduction
In view of the governments policy to strengthen the capacity at
district level to plan and implement programmes in the health
sector, including a (new) orientation towards and attention for
nutrition activities, it is envisaged that cadres should be
identified, able to fulfill this role. Given the present context,
where graduates in the field of nutrition are hardly available,
and even if they were, would not fit in with government staffing
norms for other sectors at district level, another, low.r level
type of cadre is needed. However, at present it is not clear which
existing categories of cadres would best meet the requirements or
whether a completely new type of cadre is needed.
The ccnsultancy is proposed to review the various options for
producing cadres with the required qualifications, l.e. either
through additional in-service training, through inc.usion of
specific options within ongoing training programmes or through the
set-up of a completely new training programme.
The consultant is expected to:
1. Define the types of skills needed by cadres, who would be made
responsible for planning and management of nutrition activities at
district level.
2. Review the various options for producing the cadres needed in
the most cost-effective manner and within the shortest time
possible.
More specifically the consultant is expected to:
* Identify existing categories of cadres who would come closest
to meeting the requirements.
* Indicate type of additional training needed by these cadres,
in terms of training content, level and duration.
OR, alternatively, if it does not seem opportune to make use of
existing cadres, to:
* design a new training programme (or a specific option for
inclusion in an ongoing training programme), in terms of training
content, level and duration.
I. Identify training institutes with a capacity to implement the
proposed training and assess implications in terms of resources
(manpower, physical facilities, funds)
4. Develop a curriculum for the proposed training.
5. Draw up a comprehensive training plan, in terms of numbers of
cadres to be trained, time-frame, costs, organisation and parties
involved.



- 109 -
ANNEX 3 PART 10
Page 2 of 2
In addition the consultant is requested to:
1. Assess the role of community-based extension workers operating
at a level just below the district and indicate how these workers
can be utilised in nutrition activities.
2. Identify training needed by these cadres for better performance
of nutrition-related tasks.
3. Identify training institutes with a capacity to implement the
proposed in-service training.
4. Develop a curriculum
5. Draw up a comprehensive training plan (see 5. above)

PROTRCTIG, PROMTTIEG AND SUPPORTIN  BRUSTPROUG
Exerpts frmn k Joint  IOElUICEP Statemtent, M80, GeSeva, 1989                 Ten steps
to successful breast-feeding
Every facility providing maternity services and care for
newborn infants should:
1. Have a written breast-feeding policy that is routinely
communicated to all health carc starf.
2. Train all health care staff in skills necessary to imple-
ment this policy.
3. Inform all pregnant women about the benefits and
management of breast-feeding.
4. Help mothers initirae breast-feeding within a half-hour
of birth.
S. Show mothers how to breast-feed, and how to maintain _
lactation even if ihey should bc separatcd from their
infants.
6. Give newborn infants no food or drink other than
breast milk, unless nedically indicated.
7. Practise rooming-in - allow mothers and infants to
remain together - 24 hours a day.
8. Encourage breast-feeding on demand.
9. Give no artificial teats or pacifiers (also called dummics
or soothers) to breast-feeding infants.
10. Foster the establishmeni of breast-feeding support
groups and refer mothers to them.i on discharge fromn
the hospital or clinic.

SECOND FAMILY EiEALTH PROJECT
PHYSICAL PLAYNING ADVISER
DRAFT TERMS OF REFERENCE
The Adviser will form part of the MOH Project Management
Unit and will be responsible to the Project Coordinator.
He (or she) should be an architect with extensive experience
of health tjildings in developing countries.
His duties will be to act as adviser to MOH on all matters
related to the FHP Phane II civil works.
He will be responsible for day-to-day contacts with MOPCNH,
consultants and other technical ministries or government
departments as the need arises.
The adviser will work together with a counterpart to be
appointed by GOZ. He will be responsible for drawing up a
proposal for counterpart training during the first 3 months
of his appointment and reach agreement on this with the
Project Coordinator.
It will envisaged that the Adviser will work full-time on
the project during a period of 2 years. This would be
followed by intermittent supervisory visits during 3 years
when his day-to-day duties will be taken over by the
counterpart.
BRIEFING STAGE
The Adviser will prepare written briefs on user
requirements, taking into account financial, staffing and
other possible constraints. The briefs will be illustrated
by simple sketches.
He will obtain approval of briefs from users and the Project
Management Committee before instructing MOPCNH/consultants
to proceed with designs.
Together with necessary expertise, he will review the
proposed sites for suitability for the planned development.
He will prepare approximate cost estimates and keep PHU
fully informed of cost development and cost implications of
alternative design options.



- 121 -
ANNEX 4 PART 3
Page 2 of 3
He will advise PHU on approval of appointment by MOPCNH of
consultants and their terms of reference.
DESIGNITENDER D--,UMENT STAGE
*    Agree on a work plan and time schedule for this stage
together with MOPCNH/consultants.
Provide all necessary information on requirements to
MOPCNH/consultants.
Attend planning meetings with MOPCNH/consultants as the
client/user representatives and report back to PMU with
recommendations and to obtain approval for decisions to be
taken.
*    Review cost estimates prepared by the QS and keep PHU
informed.
Ensure that MOPCNH/consultants' proposals conform with MOH
requirements.
Coordinate equipment requirements with provision of physical
facilities.
Discuss and obtain client/user approval of the final sketch
design including detailed room function drawings.
Agree with MOPCNH/consultants on contractors to be invited
to tender.
Familiarize HOPCNH/consultants with IBRD guidelines for
tendering and ensure that these are complied with.
Assist in the evaluation of tenders.
CONSTRUCTION STAGE
*    Check contract documents and iniurance coverage.
Advise PMU on acceptance or otherwise of variation orders
that MOPCNM/consultat.ts may wish to issue. Explain cost
implications and justifications for these.
*    Act as client/user representative at site meetings.  Report
to PHU on any issues which may arise.
*    Receive progress and financial reports from
MOPCNH/consultants on behalf of MOH and keep PMU informed.

Ensure that the intentions of the brief are complied with
throughout the construction period.
Together with MOPCNY/consultants inspect buildings for
handing over. Participate in handing-over meetings.
Liaise closely with MOB procurement staff to ensure
coordination of construction program with the time schedule
for commissioning.
Check compatibility of equipment and furniture with the
physical facilities being provided.

TERMS OF REFERENCE
HEALTH MANPOWER COMPONENT
LONG-TERM ADVISOR TO THE MANPOWER TASKFORCE (NATIONAL LEVEL SUPPORT)
OVERALL ROLE
Under the leadership and guidance of the Manpower Task Force, to
strengthen the capacity of the MOH to develop integrated service,
manpower and financial planning processes, focusing on improving cost
effectiveness in the training, deployment and utilization of health
personnel.
DURATION 1-2 YEARS
SPECIFIC RESPONSIBILITIES
1.    To assist the Manpower Task Force to determine priority manpower
areas for review and to develop annual strategies, and workplans.
2.    To assist in the identification of critical areas of manpower
shortage and in the development of affordable strategies and
implementation plans to address these problem areas.
3     To assist Head Office Departments in assessing the p .ential for
increasing the efficiency and effectiveness of their existing
workforce and in developing strategies for improvements in such
areas as role adaptations, working procedures, supervislon,
training, career structures, etc.
4.    To assist Head Office Department in the conduct of functional
analyses for specified staff cadres to promote effective use of
existing staff to achieve priority service targets.
5.    To assist individual Departments and the MH0 as a whole, to define
performance indicators for manpower, to develop the necessary
information support, and to use the indicators for planning,
monitoring and day-to-day management decision making.
6.    To liaise and coordinate all work at the Head Office level with
the work of the second Long Term Advisor responsible for
Provincial and District support.
7.    To assist the second long-term advisor, as required, in Provincial
and District support.
6.    To assist the Task Force in identifying short-term consultancy
requirements and in coordinating and monitoring the work of such
consultants.



- 128 -
ANNEX 5 PART 4
Page 2 of 2
9.    To assist the Task Force to coordinate and monitor all
Departmental efforts and contributions, and to integrate these
into a cohesive programme.
QUALIFICATION & EXPERIENCE
1.    At least 10 years' senior level experience in health services
planning and management of which at least 3 years should have been
gained in the developing world.
2.    Post-graduate qualification in health services planning or
management.
3.    Previous experience in human resource management highly desirable.

TERMS OF REFERENCE
HEALTH MANPOWER COMPONENT
LONG-TERH ArVISOR FOR CURRICULUM
There will be need to revise the existing health curricula to meet the
present needs and develop new curricula for new training programmes
including in-service Training. The main objective will be to develop
curricula that lead to competency-based programmes that are responsive
to health needs and services.
ROLE AND DURATION
The advisor will be based in the Health Manpower Development for a
period of two years attached to the Health Training Coordination Unit.
He/She will have the Health Training Coordinator as counterpart and will
be responsible to the Director, Health Manpower Development.
SPECIFIC RESPONSIBILITIES
1.   Work with a core group task force made up of representatives from
Health Manpower Development, Nursing Directorate, Nutrition,
Pharmacy, Public Health Laboratory and Environmental Health
Services, to review and develop curricula for training programmes
in these areas.
2.    He/She will assist the group in reviewing curricula and also
identifying core curriculum for Multidisciplinary approach to
training.
3.    To assist the group in writing/formulating appropriate curricula.
4.    To assist the core group in designing competency based training
and in developing appropriate evaluation and monitoring systems.
5.    To assist the various cadres in initiating pilot courses which
will be closely monitored, evaluated and then used as models for
the development of other training programmes.
6.    Tc assist in She design and development of training materials.
QUALIFICATIONS
1.    A Masters or PHD degree in curriculum development
2.    A minimum of five years of relevant experience.
3.    A working knowledge of competency-based, community oriented,
multidisciplinary education will be an added advantage.
4.    Previous experiense in a developing country is desirable.

ZIMBABWE
SECOND FAMILY HEALTH PROJECT
MEDICAL EQUIPMENT MAINTENANCE ADVISOR
DRAFT TERMS OF REFERENCE
GENERAL DESCRIPTION
The Medical Equipment Maintenance Advisor will be appointed for
two years to refocus and strengthen the existing program at Parirenyatwa
Hospital for provincial medical equipment maintenance technicians. This
will be done by redesigning training curricula to make it more specific
to medical needs as compared to existing one which is general. In
addition, the Advisor will supervise the up-grading of existing training
facilities at Parirenyatwa through construction and
acquisition/replacement of training equipment. The Advisor will provide
direction to the training of district handymen by provincial maintenance
technicians, by designing the associated training materials.
REPORT'NG
Reports to The Director, Medical Equipment Maintenance Department
of the Ministry of Health.
SPECIFIC RESPONSIBILITIES
The Advisor will, inter alia:
1.    Head the medical equipment maintenance training program at
Parirenyatwa.
2.    Redesign existing program to give it a health focus.
3.    Supervise the physical up-grading and re-equipping of existing
facilities.
4.    Participate in the selection of students into the program.
5.    Advise on the recruitment of two expatriate maintenance
technicians.
6.    Design and supervise programs for district handymen by provincial
maintenance technicians.
7.    Advise on the purchase of eight maintenance vehicles with
complementary toolJmaintenance kits for the provinces.
8.    Provide input into the strengthening of the materials management
program for District Health Administrators at the Harare
Polytechnic.



- 132 -
ANNEX 6 PART 1
Page 2 of 2
9.    Design and implement an in-country/overseas training program for
his counterpart.
10.   Develop and implement a management information system for
acquisition, storage and use of medical equipment at the district,
provincial, and headquarters level.
11.   Develop policies and manuals on equipment repair and maintenance
for district, provincial and headquarters staff.
QUALIFICATIONS
1.    Recognized degree/diploma in medical equipment maintenance.
2.    Several years experience in the training of medical equipment
maintenance technicians.
3.    A developing country experience will be an added advantage.

ANNEX 6 PART 2
Page 1 of 2
ZIMBABWE
SECOND FAMILY HEALTH PROJECT
FINANCIAL MANAGEMENT ADVISOR
DRAFT TERMS OF REFERENCE
BACKGROUND
A Financial Advisor will be appointed for three years to assist in
implementing the recommendations of recent studies on cost recovery,
financial decentralization and strengthening of distric. financial
management, as well as other health finance initiatives that MOH may
wish to undertake.
REPORTING
The Advisor will be responsible to the Deputy Secretary Finance
and Administration. For operational purposes, he/she will work with the
Finance Department.
SPECIFIC RESPONSIBILITIES
The Advisor will, inter alia:
1.    Provide the professional leadership in carrying out the financial
reforms entailed in ZIMBABWE: ISSUES IN THE FINANCING OF HEALTH
SERVICES (1990).
2.    Help recruit/supervise the work of short term consultants in
specific areas that required special attention as the
implementation of the reforms takes place.
3.    Help implement the recommendations arising out of the
consultanci.  through training development of manuals, workshops,
etc.
4.    Monitor financial management systems in place and ensure that
Ministry of Health finance/health management and planning staff
have the capabilities to continue with the monitoring after he/she
departs.
The specific terms of reference are tos
1.    Train district/provincial management teams as well as headquarters
accounting staff in concepts, procedures, guidelines, etc. for
financial management decentralization.



- 134 -
ANNEX 6 PART 2
Page 2 of 2
2.    Train district/provincial/headquarters accounting staff in
financial planning and preparation of estimates based on new
budget forms.
3.    Design/implement incentive systems to ensure maximization of
revenue collection at the provincial/district/health center
levels.
4.    Implement a management control system to monitor revenues.
5.    Design/implement a goal oriented/cost-effective subvention
mechanisms for MOH allocations to NGOs/municipal/district council
health facilities.
6.    Assume any other relevant responsibilities that may be assigned by
the Deputy Secretary.
QUALIFICATIONS
1.    A graduate degree in economics/finance/health management or a
recognized professional accountancy/qualification.
2.    Some practical exposure to financial issues in developing
countries.

ANNEX 6 Part 3
ZIMBASWE
SECOND FAMILY HEALTH PROJECT
PROJECT MANAGEMENT ADVISOR
DRAFT TERMS OF REFERENCE
BACKGROUND
Since FHP2 entails complex coordination, monitoring, and reporting
activities, it has been agreed ? at the Project Management Unit would
benefit greatly from the experience of a seasoned Project Management
Advisor. The Advisor, who will have had hands-on experience in managing
similar projects in other developing countries, will provide short-term
inputs (total of 6 person-months) to the PMU during the first and second
year of project implementation.
RESPONSIBILITIES
The Advisor will report to the FHP2 Project Manager. His/her
responsibilities will be, inter alia, to:
1.    Design a management information system for monitoring and
reporting the progress of various project components.
2.    Design a training program in project start-up/implementation for
component managers.
3.    Provide guidance to PMU on the design/implementation of reporting
formats for component managers.
4.    Advise on work plan scheduling to ensure that project objectives
and targets are met.
5.    Instruct PMU staff in component evaluation/feedback techniques.
6.    Advise on the design of reporting systems to meet donor
requirements.
7.    Advise on the aanagement of project accounts in conformity with
management needs and donor requirements.
8.    Help in the design/implementation of systems for monitoring
disbursements of donor funds.
9.    Undertake any other project related activity that may be assigned
by the manager, PMU.
QUALIFICATIONS
1.    A relevant University degree plus a postgraduate training in a
field relevant to project management.
2.    At least five years experience in project management at a senior
level.

ANNEX 6 Part 4
ZIMBABWE
SECOND FAMILY HEALTH PROJECT
MEDICAL EQUIPMENT SPECIALIST
DRAFT TERMS OF REFERENCE
BACKGROUND
A Medical Equipment Advisor will be appointed for a total of 6
person-months, to assist MOH in refocusing and strengthening the
procurement organization and processes for FHP2.
RESPONSIBILITIES
The Advisor will report to the FHP2 Manager. His/her
responsibilities will be, inter alia, to:
1.   Advise on the total project procurement process.
2.    Advise, support, and train the Equipment Procurement Officer over
the range of his/her activities.
3.    Review current procedures and systems and redesign and develop
these as necessary.
4.    Development and implement management information systems for
project procurement and inventory control.
5.    Develop computerized procurement systems.
6.    Advise, support, and participate in the Project Equipment
Procurement Committee in scheduling, specifying, and adjudicating
equipment.
7.    Advise and participate in equipment acceptance evaluations.
8.    Advise on storage, distribution, installation, and commissioning
of furniture and equipment.
9.    Conduct in-house staff training and advise on external training
requirements of Commissioning Unit staff.
QUALIFICATIONS
1.    Recognized degree and professional qualification.
2.    At least 10 years experience in procurement of medical equipment,
preferably including work in developing countries.

ANNEX 6 PART 5
PROJECT ADVISORY COMMITTEE
DRAFT TERMS OF REFERENCE
BACKGROUND
In order to facilitate implementation and maximize the development
impact of the Second Family Health Project, a broad-based Project
A' isory Committee (PAC) with representation from various implementing
departments will be constituted and will meet regularly, probably on a
quarterly basis.
The PAC will have the following membership:
Chairperson       Permanent Secretary or Principal Medical
Director
Deputy Chair      FHP2 Manager
Other Members     Heads of key MOH Departments (Maternal and Child
Health, Health Manpower, Health Planning and
Management, Administration/Finance, Nursing,
etc.)
ZNFPC Executive Director
Senier officials of other implementing agencies
(e.g., Ministry of Public Construction, Ministry
of Cooperatives and Community Development, etc.)
RESPONSIBILITIES
The main functions of the PAC will be tot
1.    Ensure that the goals, objectives and activitipi of the Second
Family Health Project are understood and widely known by each
department head and personnel.
2.    Determine how each department can best implement and support the
work of FHP2.
3.    Lobby at national, provincial, district and local levels, where
appropriate, for full participation and support of for the
project.
4.    Review the progress of the various components of FHP2 and advise
on needed adjustments in order to strengthen and improve
activities.
5.    Review and make recommendations on the managerial aspects of the
project.
6.    Review financial requirements and utilization of funds, to ensure
that adequate resources are available for project activities.

ANNEX 7 PART 1

ZIMBABWE
Second Family Health Pro,.-t:
Some Lessons From FHP1 Im lementation
I. Overall Project Planning
Lesson l To engage fully the interest and commitment of the provincial
and district health workers, they must be fully involved in project
planning from the beginning.
Results FHP2 planning began 18 months before appraisal, with each of
the 16 target districts asked to develop proposals which went through 3-
5 drafts.
Lesson 2: Project planning must be broad-based and participatory at the
headquarters level.
Result: A Project Planning Committee with representation of all the
major departments was formed in May 1989, and this committee spearheaded
the project preparation process.
Lesson 3: Given the magnitude of the project, it must be planned in the
context of the overall sectoral program for health and population.
Results FHP was planned together with the five-year development program
for the health sector. The World Bank sponsored the preparation of a
national strategy and implementation plan for family planing, within
which FHP2 support for population activities was located. Similar
national strategies/programs were developed for health management,
nursing services, manpower, health education, and nutrition, thus
contributing heavily to the improvement of planning skills in MOH.
II. Distr!ct Hospitals and Rural Health Centers
Lesson 1: A number of buildings in the FHP hospitals were over-designed
(e.g., laundry, kitchen, operating theater).
Results A functional design review of all eight hospitals was carried
out in mid-1990, and dramatically new and less costly designs were
developed and accepted by MOH for FHP2. The 16 district hospital
upgrades in the second project are expected to cost about the same
amount as the eight hospitals in the first project.
Lesson 2i The inflexible design of the hospitals (all 140 beds) in FHPI
was not responsive to local conditions in the districts.
Result: A flexible, modular design was adopted for FHP2, leading to
hospitals with 52, 78, 104, and 120 beds, plus a variety of options for
operating theaters, pharmacy, etc,., depending on local needs.
Lesson 3: The award of the contract for eight hospitals to one
contractor and simultaneous construction of all facilities in FHP1



- 139 -
ANNEX 7 PART I
Page 2 of 5
resulted in cumbersome supervision arrangements and put a strain on the
construction industry.
Results For FHP2, construction will be staggered over five years, and
the job will be broken down into smaller bid packages.
Lesson 4: Tendering for medical equipment on an item-by-item basis was
administratively burdensome and led to some incompatibility of
equipment.
Result: FHP2 equipment bids will be evaluated on a lot-by-lot basis and
contracts awarded for entire lots. All equipment lists and procurement
procedures will be reviewed before FHP2 gets under way in late 1991.
Lesson 5s Some features of the rural health centers in FHP1 were not
cost-efficient (e.g., malelfemale holding wards).
Resultt These items are being deleted or modified in the designs for
FHP2. A flexible modular design has been adopted.
Lesson 6: The improved maternity services at the upgraded RHCs
(delivery room and equipment) have not been fully utilized thus far,
because of the nationwide shortage of trained nurse-midwives.
Result: In FHP2, a major program to expanded and improve the training
of midwives is being launched.
III. Health Transport and Communications
Lesson 1: While FHPI vehicles have generally been kept on the road, the
shortage of spare parts and lack of prompt maintenance by the Central
Mechanical Equipment Department has hampered their use.
Result: The World Bank and other donors have indicated that their level
of support for health transport will depend on whether the Government
changes its current policies on CMED maintenance. It is now reported
that Government is changing this policy; the World Bank team is
following up.
Lesson 2: The PTC has repeatedly failed to installed telephones in the
rural health centers as promised.
Results In view of the importance of having a communications link
between RECs and the district hospitals, point-to-point radio
communications systems will be provided in FHP2.
IV. MCH/FP Training
Lesson l In order to plan and carry out in-service training in a
coordinated and effective manner, the provinces and iistricts themselves
must plan and budget for the training on an annual basis.
Results Provincial training coordinators are being appointed, and
district-level training committees are being charged with the task of
setting annual training plans.



- i40 -
ANNEX 7 PART 1
Page 3 of 5
Lesson 2: It is not easy to monitor and document expenditures for
small, scattered in-service training activities which are reimbursable
by the donors.
Results Annual district training plans are now starting to identify the
source of funds, and district staff are being assisted by the Project
Management Department in claiming donor funds on a reimbursable basis.
Consequently, reimbursements for training are accelerating, e.g.,
Netherlands disbursements have increased from DFO.5 million in 1989 to
about DFl.5 million in 1990.
Lesson 3:  The large numb   of short in-service courses need to be
closely coordinated and combined where possible, so that staff are not
drawn away from their work unnecessarily.
Result: The training coordinator in the Manpower Department, along with
provincial and district trainers, are reviewing in-service courses and
rationalizing them.
Lesson 4: Tutors, once trained, will only be retained if they have
established posts and receive a higher grade and pay to go along with
their new skills/responsibilities.
Result: A pay increase for nurse tutors has just been approved, and the
upgrading of district MCH/FP trainers will be a conditionality for FHP2.
Lesson 5: Training is only fully effective when trainers are able to
follow-up and supervise trainees.
Result: Additional funds will be provided in FHP2 for supervision and
transport.
Lesson 6: Given the large numbers of trainees involved, unit costs for
training need to be carefully estimated to avoid major miscalculations
of funds required for training.
Result:  Training costs FHP2 are being estimated in great detail, using
the actual costs of training (travel, accommodation, subsistence,
teaching, etc.) in FHPI districts.
Lesson 7: It was ill-advised to rely heavily on another ministry
(Cooperatives and Community Development) to organize and support a major
part of the FHP training program.
Results FHP2 support to MCCD is being reviewed. At the same time,
increasing emphasis is being given to recruitment and training of ether
community-based workers (e.g., CBDs, ward nutrition coordinators, etc.)
V.    Family Planning
Lesson ls To keep up the momentum of the family planning program, basic
services must be extended to those rural areas not yet covered
effectively by ZNFPC and MOH programs.
Results In FHP2, the CBD program will be expanded by 200-300 community
workers assigned to as-yet-uncovered parts of Zimbabwe. At the same
time, in-service training of nurses in HCH/FP will be accelerated.



- 141 -
ANNEX 7 PART 1
Page 4 of 5
Lesson 2: The FHP1 family planning activities neglected young people,
despite the fact that teen-age pregnancies are increasino And the demand
for FP services among adolescents is high.
Result:  Family Planning in FHP2 will focus especially on Youth Advisory
Services, with the addition of staff, facilities, and IEC campaigns
targeted at young people.
Lesson 3: Past efforts to increase family planning acceptance were too
heavily concentrated on the use of oral contraceptives. To maintain the
momentum of the FP program, a diversified miz of methods must be
offered, starting with the urban areas.
Result: Building on the pilot efforts in VSC in FHP1, an expanded
program for use of semi-permanent and permanent methods (IUD, Norplant,
Depo-Provera, VSC) has been developed for FHP2. This will be
implemented in close cooperation with USAID.
VI. Information, Education, and Communication CIEC)
Lesson 1: Chronic shortages of ink and paper have inhibited production
of print materials.
Result: Donor funds will be used in FHP2 to import these materials, as
necessary.
Lesson 2: Effective design and dissemination of IEC materials cannot be
handled by the head office only; provincial and district involvement is
required.
Result: The ZNFPC is appointing provincial IEC officers; small IEC
units are being established at provincial level; and the Health
Education Unit is decentralizing materials design and production to the
provinces.
Lesson 3: While mass media campaigns are an important part of IEC,
there is also a pressing need to develop training materials for service
providers in communications and counselling, as well as materials for
these providers to use in communicating with clients.
Result: ZEC materials for training for use by service providers are
being included as an integral part of FHP2.
VII. Management of Health Services
Lesson l While there were important advances in health management
under FHP1 (especially through the establishment of the District Health
Services Administrators course), several management sub-systems were not
adequately tackled.
Result: In FHP2, management strengthening will concentrate on financial
systems/skills/policies and on the improved management of medical
equipment, materials, and transport.



- 142 -
ANNEX 7 PART 1
Page 5 of 5
Lesson 2: Even though health planning skills at district and provincial
levels improved in FHPI (and as a result of the planning for FHP2
itself), this was not linked to the development of budgeting and
financial control systems at these levels.
Results A major element of management strengthening in FHP2 will be the
development district-level financial skills and systems.
Lesson 3:  The senior managers of MOH were not fully-involved in
management strengthening in FHPl. This diluted the effectiveness of the
program.
Result:  The MOH top management team have participated heavily in FHP2
preparation, and will themselves undergo management training and analyze
management issues as part of FHP2 implementation.
VIII. Proiect Management
Lesson 1 Given the size and complexity of the project, strong
management systems need to be established at the outset, agreed to by
all component managers, and continuously refined.
Result: FHPl management systems are being upgraded for FHP2; a major
work-planning/project launch workshop will be held in mid-1991, before
FHP2 gets under way.
Lesson 2: Project finances need to be rigorously tracked from the
outset, and streamlined procedures for processing reimbursement claims
must be developed.
Result: A project financial assistant will be appointed for FHP2, to
work with the existing project accountant.
Lesson 3: It is essential that MOH have a full-time physical
plannerlarchitect among its staff, to develop the health facilities
construction program, monitor its progress, and generally liaise
effectively with Ministry of Construction and consulting architects.
Results A physical planner/architect will join the Project Department
as soon as possible, ideally during the first half of 1991.

ZIMBABWE: SECOND FAMILY HEALTH PROJECT
SUPERVISION PLAN
1.    Borrower's Contribution to Supervision
(a)   Progress reports are to be submitted to the Bank every six months
(in April and October) by the Project Management Unit (PMU) within
MOH.
(b)   Project monitoring and coordination will be the responsibility of
the PMU, and the Project Advisory Committee (consisting of the
Project Coordinator and DEputy, and Heads or representatives of
ZNFPC, the Departments of MCH and Health Manpower and the Nursing
Directorate, the MOH planner/s, and the Committee Secretary) which
will meet at least monthly. Additional people, with
respousibility for implementation of parts of the project
(including ZNFPC Unit Heads, the Chiefs of the Nutrition and HEU
Units) will be invited to these meetings as appropriate.
(c)   The Project Coordinator and/or Deputy Coordinator will meet at
least quarterly with the Provincial Medical Directors, to review
project progress and plans.
(d)   ZNFPC's Responsibility  While the PMU and MOH have responsibility
for the entire project, including the parts of the family planning
component which are to be implemented by the ZNFPC, routine
supervision and monitoring of the family planning component will
be carried out by ZNFPC through its existing management structure.
Project progress and issues will be the main agenda item of at
least one meeting each month of the Executive Director and Unit
Heads of ZNFPC. ZNFPC will provide quarterly reports to the PMU,
including financial statements for the project.
(e)   The PMU will be responsible for coordinating arrangements for Bank
supervision missions and for providing information required by
missions. Missions will normally be accompanied by an officer
from the MOH, the PMU and ZNFPC.
(f)   Mission briefing meetings on arrival and wrap-up meetings before
departure will normally be chaired by the Secretary for Health.
ZNFPC will also arrange (in consultation with the PMU) a briefing
meeting for the mission, normally chaired by the Executive Head of
the Council.
2.    Bank Supervision Inputs   It is estimated that regular supervision
from Washington (to review progress reports, procurement actions,
correspondence, etc) will require five staff-weeks in the first two
years of the project and four staff-weeks each year thereafter. The
staff time in the table which follows is in addition to this day-to-day
supervision.
